[0:0:66,13] 2021-22 STATE BUDGET — HHS   178 

[1:0:419,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[2:0:170,32] 5160   Department of Rehabilitation - Continued 

[3:0:66,66] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[4:0:66,85] 4210 - VOCATIONAL REHABILITATION SERVICES  

[5:0:66,103] The Vocational Rehabilitation Services Program delivers vocational rehabilitation services to persons with disabilities through  

[5:1:66,113] vocational rehabilitation professionals in district and branch offices located throughout the state so that persons with disabilities  

[5:2:66,123] may prepare for and engage in competitive integrated employment and achieve economic self-sufficiency. In addition, the  

[5:3:66,133] Department has cooperative agreements with state and local agencies (secondary and postsecondary education, behavioral/ 

[5:4:66,143] mental health, and welfare) to provide services to consumers. The Department operates under a federal Order of Selection  

[5:5:66,154] process, which gives priority to persons with the most significant disabilities.  

[6:0:66,171] Persons with disabilities who are eligible for the Department's vocational rehabilitation services may be provided a full range of  

[6:1:66,181] services, including vocational assessment, assistive technology, vocational and educational training, job placement, supported  

[6:2:66,192] employment and independent living skills training to maximize their ability to live and work independently within their  

[6:3:66,202] communities. The Department provides Work Incentives Planning services to reduce dependency on public benefits. The  

[6:4:66,212] Department provides career counseling and information and referral services to encourage individuals working in non-

[6:5:66,222] competitive, non-integrated settings to work toward and achieve competitive integrated employment.  

[7:0:66,240] The Department additionally provides pre-employment transition student services, known as DOR Student Services, and  

[7:1:66,250] auxiliary aids and services necessary to participate in such services to a wide range of students with disabilities, ages 16 up to  

[7:2:66,260] 22 (depending on their exit from their special education program), including many who may benefit from early career  

[7:3:66,271] development. DOR Student Services include job exploration counseling, work-based learning experiences, postsecondary  

[7:4:66,281] education counseling, workplace readiness training, and instruction in self-advocacy. 

[8:0:66,298] The Department, through its Business Enterprises Program, provides comprehensive training and technical assistance to  

[8:1:66,309] enable persons who are blind or visually impaired to support themselves in the operation of vending stands, snack bars, and  

[8:2:66,319] cafeterias. Prevocational, including employment readiness, services are provided by the Orientation Center for the Blind to  

[8:3:66,329] consumers with vision loss to prepare them for independent living.  

[9:0:66,347] The Department works with public and private organizations to develop and improve community-based vocational rehabilitation  

[9:1:66,357] services for the Department's consumers. The Department sets standards, certifies Community Rehabilitation Programs, and  

[9:2:66,367] establishes fees for services provided to its consumers.  

[10:0:66,385] The Department works with the federal government to administer the California Career Innovations Demonstration Project to  

[10:1:66,395] identify how to increase the self-sufficiency of students with disabilities by providing work-based learning experiences and  

[10:2:66,405] planned education to prepare them for workplace success.  

[11:0:66,423] 4215 - INDEPENDENT LIVING SERVICES  

[12:0:66,441] The Department funds, administers, and supports 28 non-profit independent living centers in communities located throughout  

[12:1:66,451] California. Each independent living center provides services necessary to assist consumers to live independently   with full  

[12:2:66,461] inclusion   in their communities. Core services consist of information and referral, peer counseling, individual and systems  

[12:3:66,471] change advocacy, independent living skills, housing assistance, personal assistance referral services, transition and diversion  

[12:4:66,481] services to community based living, and   transition services to postsecondary life for youth.  

[13:0:66,499] The Department administers and supports the Traumatic Brain Injury (TBI) Program. In coordination with consumers and their  

[13:1:66,509] families, seven service providers throughout California provide a coordinated post-acute care service model for persons with  

[13:2:66,520] TBI, including supported living, community reintegration, vocational supportive services, public awareness, and support for  

[13:3:66,530] family, friends, and professionals within the TBI community. The Department also works with the federal government to  

[13:4:66,540] administer a TBI partnership grant with which a state TBI Advisory Board has been established for the purpose of creating a  

[13:5:66,550] statewide TBI registry, needs assessment, and resource plan.  

[14:0:66,568] The Department administers the federal Older Individuals Who Are Blind program that supports 17 non-profit community-based  

[14:1:66,578] organizations throughout California that provide blindness-related independent living services necessary to assist visually  

[14:2:66,588] impaired consumers age 55 or older to live independently and be productive in their communities. Core services consist of low  

[14:3:66,598] vision evaluations/screenings, assistive technology devices and training, orientation and mobility, communication skills,  

[14:4:66,609] independent living skills training, self-advocacy, adjustment counseling, transportation, and supportive services.  

[15:0:66,626] 9900 - ADMINISTRATION  

[16:0:66,647] The Administration Program provides overall management planning, policy development, and administrative support services  

[16:1:66,657] to departmental programs.  

[17:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[5:1:66,250] 4250 - STATE COUNCIL SERVICES  

[6:0:66,270] The State Independent Living Council, in conjunction with the Department of Rehabilitation, is responsible for developing a  

[6:1:66,280] state plan for independent living and for monitoring, reviewing and evaluating the implementation of that plan. The Council also  

[6:2:66,290] interacts with similar statewide councils to enhance the effectiveness of the network of centers that provide independent living  

[6:3:66,301] services in California. The Council is required by the Federal Rehabilitation Act of 1973, as amended, in order for the state to  

[6:4:66,311] receive financial assistance for Independent Living Services and the Centers for Independent Living. The Council serves as an  

[6:5:66,321] educational resource on disability and independent living for the Governor, other state agencies, the Legislature, the general  

[6:6:66,331] public, and a variety of statewide and national organizations.

[0:0:66,13] 2021-22 STATE BUDGET — HHS   188 

[1:0:419,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[2:0:144,32] 5175   Department of Child Support Services - Continued 

[3:0:66,66] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[3:1:66,85] 4260 - CHILD SUPPORT SERVICES PROGRAM  

[4:0:66,103] The Child Support Services program establishes the system and process for encouraging and, when necessary, enforcing  

[4:1:66,113] parental responsibilities by establishing paternity for children, establishing court orders for financial and medical support, and  

[4:2:66,123] enforcing those orders. The program operates as the single state entity designed to administer the federally mandated Title IV-

[4:3:66,133] D child support program in California. Operation of this program is required for the state to continue to receive the Temporary  

[4:4:66,143] Assistance for Needy Families block grant.  

[4:5:66,161] 4260010 - CHILD SUPPORT ADMINISTRATION:  

[5:0:66,179] The Child Support Administration program provides funding for the salaries and benefits for local and state staff, and operating  

[5:1:66,189] expenses and equipment for the operation of California's child support program, including local child support agencies. The  

[5:2:66,199] federal government provides 66 percent of the funding and the state funds 34 percent of the administration costs.  

[5:3:66,217] 4260019 - CHILD SUPPORT AUTOMATION:  

[6:0:66,235] Pursuant to Federal law, the Department created a single, statewide child support automation system that meets federal  

[6:1:66,245] certification. There are two components of the statewide system: the Child Support Enforcement system and the State  

[6:2:66,255] Disbursement Unit. The enforcement system provides local child support staff tools to manage child support customer accounts  

[6:3:66,265] and locate and intercept assets of non-custodial parents delinquent in their child support payments. The Child Support  

[6:4:66,275] Automation program provides funding for the vendor-operated state disbursement unit, which collects child support payments  

[6:5:66,286] from non-custodial parents and disburses payments to custodial parties. In addition, the Child Support Automation program  

[6:6:66,296] provides funding for electronic data processing maintenance and operation costs at local agencies.  

[7:0:66,336] DETAILED EXPENDITURES BY PROGRAM

[4:0:66,116] MAJOR PROGRAM CHANGES  

[5:0:65,135] • Community Care Expansion Program—The Budget includes $805 million in 2021-22 for the construction, acquisition and/or  

[5:1:76,145] rehabilitation of projects to preserve or expand adult and senior care facilities to serve people experiencing homelessness or  

[5:2:76,156] who are at risk of becoming homeless.  

[6:0:65,172] • Project Roomkey—The Budget includes $150 million one-time General Fund to support transitioning participants into  

[6:1:76,182] permanent housing.  

[7:0:65,198] • Home Safe—The Budget includes $92.5 million General Fund in both 2021-22 and 2022-23 for the Home Safe program for  

[7:1:76,208] access to health, safety, and housing supports for individuals involved in or at risk of involvement in Adult Protective  

[7:2:76,219] Services.  

[8:0:65,235] • Housing and Disability Advocacy Program—The Budget includes $150 million General Fund in 2021-22 and 2022-23 to  

[8:1:76,245] assist disabled individuals who are experiencing homelessness. This augmentation is in addition to an ongoing annual  

[8:2:76,255] appropriation of $25 million General Fund for this purpose.  

[9:0:65,271] • Addressing Complex Care Needs for Foster Youth—The Budget includes $139.2 million General Fund to assist counties with  

[9:1:76,282] serving foster youth with complex needs and behavioral health conditions, within California, as well as youth that return from  

[9:2:76,292] an out-of-state congregate placement.  

[10:0:65,308] • CalWORKs Housing Support Program Investment—The Budget includes $190 million General Fund in both 2021-22 and  

[10:1:76,318] 2022-23 to expand the existing CalWORKs Housing Support program.  

[11:0:65,334] • Bringing Families Home Program—The Budget includes $92.5 million General Fund in both 2021-22 and 2022-23 (with  

[11:1:76,345] spending authority through 2024-25) to expand the existing Bringing Families Home program. This program provides  

[11:2:76,355] housing-related supports to eligible families experiencing homelessness in the child welfare system.  

[12:0:65,371] • Family Reunification CalWORKs Assistance Payment—The Budget includes $8.8 million General Fund in 2021-22 and  

[12:1:76,381] ongoing for counties to continue providing CalWORKs services for up to 180 days when a child has been removed from the  

[12:2:76,391] home and is receiving out-of-home care.  

[13:0:65,408] • Family First Prevention Services Act Part I—The Budget includes $222.5 million General Fund in 2021-22 to be expended  

[13:1:76,418] over three years to assist counties with new prevention services implementation efforts allowable under the new federal  

[13:2:76,428] Family First Prevention Services Act. These one-time resources will assist counties to build locally driven prevention services  

[13:3:76,438] and supports for children, youth and families at risk of entering foster care.  

[14:0:65,454] • Foster Care Emergency Assistance—The Budget includes $24.5 million General Fund and federal TANF block grant funds in  

[14:1:76,465] 2021-22 to provide caregivers with up to four months of emergency assistance payments pending resource family approval  

[14:2:76,475] and up to twelve months for cases that meet good cause criteria.  

[15:0:65,491] • Child Welfare Services-California Automated Response and Engagement System—The Budget includes $39.4 million  

[15:1:76,501] General Fund in 2021-22 to continue development of a new technology platform for Child Welfare Services.  

[16:0:65,517] • Child and Adolescent Needs and Strengths Assessment Tool Workload—The Budget includes $3.4 million General Fund  

[16:1:76,528] ongoing for increased county social worker workload associated with the Child and Adolescent Needs and Strengths  

[16:2:76,538] assessment tool.  

[17:0:65,554] • Continuum of Care Reform Reconciliation—The Budget includes $7.1 million General Fund to reflect Continuum of Care  

[17:1:76,564] Reform true-up related to county Child and Family Teams actual expenditures for fiscal year 2018-19.  

[18:0:65,580] • Stipend for Tribal Social Work Students—The Budget includes $3 million General Fund in 2021?22 to provide a Master of  

[18:1:76,591] Social Work Program stipend for tribal members or Native Americans who commit to working in tribal social services  

[18:2:76,601] programs dedicated to serve children and families through after graduation.  

[19:0:65,617] • CWS Augmentation—The Budget includes $85 million General Fund in one-time support for child welfare services activities.  

[20:0:65,633] • Infant Supplement—The Budget includes $1.8 million General Fund for Healthy Futures for Foster Youth.  

[21:0:65,649] • Child Welfare Caregiver Pandemic Assistance—The Budget includes $80 million General Fund one-time Child Welfare  

[21:1:76,660] Caregiver Stipend/COVID-19 Pandemic Assistance.  

[22:0:65,676] • Short-Term Residential Therapeutic Program Pandemic Assistance—The Budget includes $42 million one-time General  

[22:1:76,686] Fund for Foster Care Short-Term Residential Therapeutic Program COVID Relief.  

[23:0:65,702] • Emergency Response Social Workers—The Budget includes $50 million General Fund to support increased Emergency  

[24:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:76,69] Response Social Workers in Child Welfare.  

[4:0:65,85] • Foster Family Agencies—The Budget includes $5.4 million General Fund to increase Foster Family Agency rates by $50 per  

[4:1:76,95] child per month to reduce social worker turnover.  

[5:0:65,111] • Child Welfare Training Additional Support—The Budget includes an additional $7 million General Fund for Child Welfare  

[5:1:76,121] Training.  

[6:0:65,138] • Guaranteed Income Pilot Program—The Budget includes $35 million General Fund over five years for Guaranteed Income  

[6:1:76,148] pilot programs. These pilot programs will be city or county administered, require a local-match commitment, and target  

[6:2:76,158] former foster youth, pregnant or parenting foster youth, and low-income Californians.  

[7:0:65,174] • CalWORKs Grant Increase—The Budget reflects a 5.3-percent increase to CalWORKs Maximum Aid Payment levels, which  

[7:1:76,184] is estimated to cost $141.9 million in 2021-22. These increased grant costs are funded entirely by the Child Poverty and  

[7:2:76,195] Family Supplemental Support Subaccounts of the Local Revenue Fund.  

[8:0:65,211] • Federal Pandemic Emergency Assistance Fund—The Budget includes $204 million federal Pandemic Emergency  

[8:1:76,221] Assistance Fund/TANF to provide one-time cash payment to CalWORKs families.  

[9:0:65,237] • CalWORKs Overpayments—The Budget includes two changes to CalWORKs overpayment collections. First, beginning April  

[9:1:76,247] 2020 through the end of the pandemic or June 30, 2022, whichever is sooner, counties are authorized to consider all non-

[9:2:76,258] fraudulent overpayments as administrative errors. This will reduce required collections from inadvertent household errors  

[9:3:76,268] from ten percent to five percent of a family’s aid payments. Second, the CalWORKs Overpayment collection timeframe will  

[9:4:76,278] be reduced from five years to two years.  

[10:0:65,294] • Indian Health Clinic Funding Restoration—The Budget includes $1.9 million ongoing General Fund to restore Indian Health  

[10:1:76,304] Clinic funding to pre-2009 funding levels.  

[11:0:65,321] • IHSS State and County Sharing Ratio—The Budget includes increased state costs of $57.3 million General Fund in 2021-22  

[11:1:76,331] and $123.8 million ongoing General Fund to reflect the continuation of the 65-percent state and 35-percent county sharing  

[11:2:76,341] ratio and the continuation of the ten percent over three years option.  

[12:0:65,357] • IHSS Seven Percent Fiscal Penalty—The Budget assumes that counties will pay a one-time penalty for failing to agree to  

[12:1:76,367] contracts with IHSS providers through the collective bargaining process.  

[13:0:65,384] • Long Term Care Career Pathways—The Budget includes $200 million one-time General Fund to incentivize, support, and  

[13:1:76,394] fund career pathways for IHSS providers, allowing these workers to build on their experience to obtain a higher-level job in  

[13:2:76,404] the home care and/or health care industry.  

[14:0:65,420] • IHSS Seven Percent Suspension—The Budget eliminates the IHSS seven-percent reduction in service hours resulting in a  

[14:1:76,430] cost of approximately $248 million General Fund in 2022-23 and $496 million ongoing General Fund.  

[15:0:65,447] • IHSS Electronic Forms—The Budget includes $5 million General Fund for IHSS Electronic Forms.  

[16:0:65,463] • SSP Grant Increase—The Budget includes $291.3 million General Fund in 2021-22 and ongoing to increase grants for SSP,  

[16:1:76,473] Cash Assistance Program for Immigrants, and California Veterans Cash Benefits. Future SSP grant increases will be subject  

[16:2:76,483] to an appropriation.  

[17:0:65,499] • Adult Protective Services—The Budget includes $70 million General Fund for Adult Protective Services Expansion.  

[18:0:65,516] • Rapid Response Efforts—The Budget includes $105.2 million one-time General Fund for the Rapid Response Fund to  

[18:1:76,526] provide support for migrant family arrivals at the Southern California border and additional funding for other emergency  

[18:2:76,536] responses, including wildfires and drought.  

[19:0:65,552] • Unaccompanied Undocumented Minors (UUM)—The Budget includes $20 million General Fund in 2021-22 to provide  

[19:1:76,562] additional support for UUMs through the Opportunities for Youth pilot project ($4.7 million General Fund), the UUM legal  

[19:2:76,573] services ($14 million General Fund), and state operations ($1.3 million General Fund).  

[20:0:65,589] • California Newcomer Education and Well-Being Project (CalNEW)—The Budget includes $5 million Proposition 98 General  

[20:1:76,599] Fund in 2020-21 to assist school districts in improving refugee and UUM students' well-being, English-language proficiency,  

[20:2:76,609] and academic performance.  

[21:0:65,625] • DACA and Naturalization Filing Fees—The Budget includes $25 million one-time General Fund in 2021-22 to fund filing fees  

[21:1:76,636] for DACA and naturalization.  

[22:0:65,652] • Case Management for Asylees and Vulnerable Noncitizens—The Budget includes $8 million one-time General Fund for  

[22:1:76,662] Case Management for asylees and other vulnerable non-citizens.  

[23:0:65,678] • One California—The Budget includes $30 million one-time General Fund to augment the One California legal services  

[23:1:76,688] programs for immigrants.  

[24:0:65,705] • Community Response Initiative to Strengthen Emergency Systems (C.R.I.S.E.S) Act—The Budget includes $10 million

[1:0:419,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[2:0:166,32] 5180   Department of Social Services - Continued 

[3:0:66,66] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[4:0:66,85] 4270 - WELFARE PROGRAMS  

[5:0:66,105] The Department's public assistance programs provide financial assistance to California residents who are unable to support  

[5:1:66,115] themselves. These programs are comprised of five components:  

[6:0:65,133] • California Work Opportunity and Responsibility to Kids (CalWORKs)  

[7:0:65,149] • Other Assistance Payments, including Foster Care, Adoption Assistance Program, Refugee Cash Assistance, and Food  

[7:1:76,160] Assistance Programs  

[8:0:65,176] • Supplemental Security Income/State Supplementary Payment Program  

[9:0:65,192] • County Administration and Automation Projects  

[10:0:65,208] • Disaster Relief  

[11:0:66,236] The objectives of these programs are to provide temporary financial assistance to eligible needy and dependent persons to  

[11:1:66,246] enable achievement of self-sufficiency or to provide safe living environments for vulnerable adults and children, and to monitor,  

[11:2:66,256] administer, and improve the quality of all welfare services.  

[12:0:66,274] 4270010 - CalWORKs:  

[13:0:66,284] The CalWORKs program is California's version of the federal Temporary Assistance for Needy Families program. CalWORKs is  

[13:1:66,295] California's largest cash aid program for children and families and is designed to provide temporary assistance to meet basic  

[13:2:66,305] needs, such as shelter, food, and clothing, in times of crisis, while encouraging personal responsibility. CalWORKs includes  

[13:3:66,315] specific welfare-to-work requirements and provides supportive services, such as child care, to enable an individual to meet  

[13:4:66,325] these requirements. Child care services currently are provided through a three-stage system to current and former CalWORKs  

[13:5:66,335] recipients with children through the age of 10 (or up to 12 under certain conditions). Stage One is administered by the  

[13:6:66,346] Department of Social Services. Parents have the right to choose child care among center-based, family child care homes, or  

[13:7:66,356] license-exempt providers. CalWORKs families are then able to meet both goals of moving from welfare into the work force and  

[13:8:66,366] engaging children in child care and development services.  

[14:0:66,384] 4270019 - Other Assistance Payments:  

[15:0:66,394] The Foster Care program provides assistance payments to relatives, foster family homes, foster family agencies, short-term  

[15:1:66,404] residential treatment centers or group homes for children who have been removed from the custody of a parent or guardian as  

[15:2:66,414] a result of a judicial order or voluntary placement agreement due to findings of abuse, neglect or exploitation. This program is  

[15:3:66,424] administered by the counties in accordance with regulations, standards, and procedures set by the Department of Social  

[15:4:66,435] Services as authorized by federal and state law. The Kinship Guardianship Assistance Program provides support payments to  

[15:5:66,445] relative guardians of children who were previously in the foster care system.  

[16:0:66,465] The Adoption Assistance Program provides financial assistance to families adopting a child with special needs or to facilitate  

[16:1:66,475] the adoption of children who otherwise would remain in long-term foster care. This program is administered by the counties in  

[16:2:66,486] accordance with regulations, standards, and procedures set by the Department of Social Services as authorized by federal and  

[16:3:66,496] state law.  

[17:0:66,516] California also provides cash assistance to eligible refugee/entrant populations via the following programs:  

[18:0:65,534] • The Refugee Cash Assistance provides cash grants to refugees/entrants in their first eight months in the United States  

[18:1:76,544] provided they are not otherwise eligible for categorical welfare programs.  

[19:0:65,580] • The Unaccompanied Refugee Minors program provides culturally and linguistically appropriate child welfare, foster care, and  

[19:1:76,590] independent living services to minors who do not have parents in the United States, or who enter the United States  

[19:2:76,600] unaccompanied by a parent, an immediate adult relative, or an adult having documentable legal evidence of custody of the  

[19:3:76,610] minor.  

[20:0:65,646] • The Trafficking and Crime Victims Assistance Program provides cash aid and social services to noncitizen victims of human  

[20:1:76,656] trafficking, domestic violence and other serious crimes who meet the income and eligibility requirements. Benefits are  

[20:2:76,666] available for a maximum period of eight months for adults without children and up to 48 months for families (under  

[20:3:76,676] CalWORKs).  

[21:0:66,704] The CalFresh Program, federally referred to as the Supplemental Nutrition Assistance Program, provides improved levels of  

[21:1:66,714] nutrition among eligible low-income households by offering them a benefit amount, posted to a debit card, for the purpose of  

[22:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[0:0:66,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[1:0:407,13] 2021-22 STATE BUDGET — HHS   203 

[2:0:166,32] 5180   Department of Social Services - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] purchasing food. The cost of CalFresh benefits is provided by the United States Department of Agriculture for populations  

[3:1:66,79] eligible to receive federal benefits. Legal immigrants who meet program eligibility criteria but are ineligible for federal benefits  

[3:2:66,89] due to their immigration status are served under the state-funded program known as the California Food Assistance Program.  

[3:3:66,99] The CalFresh Employment and Training Program requires certain non-assistance CalFresh recipients to participate in  

[3:4:66,109] employment and training activities.  

[4:0:66,130] The Emergency Food Assistance Program provides commodities to local food banks in all 58 California counties for distribution  

[4:1:66,140] to the working poor, low-income, unemployed, and homeless persons. The food is distributed to eligible recipients for  

[4:2:66,150] household consumption or used to prepare and serve meals in congregate settings. This program is also supplemented with  

[4:3:66,160] food purchased by food banks using private donations, funds provided by the state, taxpayer contributions generated through a  

[4:4:66,171] state income tax check-off, as well as surplus fresh fruits and vegetables donated by farmers and businesses.  

[5:0:66,191] The Commodity Supplemental Food Program is a federally funded program for local non-profit agencies to provide nutritious  

[5:1:66,201] supplemental foods to low-income, elderly people at least 60 years of age. Administrative responsibility for the Commodity  

[5:2:66,211] Supplemental Food Program was transferred from the California Department of Education to the Department of Social Services  

[5:3:66,222] on October 1, 2016.  

[6:0:66,239] 4270020 - Child Care and Development:  

[7:0:66,257] The Child Care Development program reflects services that will transition to the Department of Social Services administration  

[7:1:66,267] from the Department of Education, effective July 1, 2021. This includes but is not limited to Stages Two and Three of child care,  

[7:2:66,277] migrant day care, and Child and Adult Care Food Programs.  

[8:0:66,295] 4270028 - Supplemental Security Income/State Supplementary Payment Program:  

[9:0:66,313] The federal Supplemental Security Income (SSI) program is a cash assistance program for low-income aged, blind, or disabled  

[9:1:66,323] persons who meet the program's income and resource requirements. California supplements the federal SSI payment with a  

[9:2:66,333] State Supplementary Payment (SSP). The SSI/SSP program is administered by the federal Social Security Administration who  

[9:3:66,343] determines eligibility, computes grants, and disburses the combined monthly payment to recipients.  

[10:0:66,361] 4270037 - County Administration and Automation Projects:  

[11:0:66,379] Federal, state, and county governments share the cost of operating expenses and the salaries and benefits of county staff who  

[11:1:66,389] administer public assistance programs.  

[12:0:66,407] Federal, state, and county funds are used to finance major data automation projects of the Department of Social Services.  

[13:0:66,424] 4270046 - Disaster Relief:  

[14:0:66,442] The objective of the Disaster Relief Program is to provide monetary assistance to individuals and households who have  

[14:1:66,452] suffered eligible losses from a Presidentially-declared disaster that are not covered by other federal, state, or private assistance  

[14:2:66,463] programs, and to oversee mass care and shelter, social services recovery, emergency repatriation, and administration of select  

[14:3:66,473] recovery grants.  

[15:0:66,490] 4275 - SOCIAL SERVICES AND LICENSING  

[16:0:66,508] The Department of Social Services oversees and monitors the administration of social services programs, which include child  

[16:1:66,518] welfare, adoptions, licensing and special programs. The department is responsible for development of policy, regulations, and  

[16:2:66,529] procedures that govern the delivery of services to children, families and other recipients, and the monitoring and evaluation of  

[16:3:66,539] the service delivery system.  

[17:0:66,556] 4275010 - In-Home Supportive Services:  

[18:0:66,574] The In-Home Supportive Services (IHSS) program provides in-home services that enable eligible individuals to remain safely in  

[18:1:66,584] their own homes as an alternative to out-of-home care. Eligible persons are low-income aged, blind, or disabled individuals who  

[18:2:66,595] either qualify for federally funded Medi-Cal or meet the program's income and resource requirements. There are four programs  

[18:3:66,605] that provide in-home care: the Personal Care Services Program, IHSS Plus Option Program, Community First Choice Option,  

[18:4:66,615] and IHSS-Residual Program.  

[19:0:66,633] 4275019 - Children and Adult Services and Licensing:  

[20:0:66,643] The Children's Services component consists of three major areas: Child Welfare Services, Adoptions, and Child Abuse  

[20:1:66,653] Prevention.  

[21:0:66,673] Child Welfare Services provides emergency response, family maintenance, family reunification, and permanent placement and  

[21:1:66,684] prevention services to protect abused, neglected or exploited children. The services are provided through an integrated  

[21:2:66,694] services delivery system that provides intensive services to families to promote child safety, permanency and well-being with  

[21:3:66,704] the goal of allowing families to stay together in their own homes, or arrangement for the child's placement in the safest and  

[21:4:66,714] least restrictive home-like setting. Services also include assistance to youth who are emancipating or have emancipated from  

[22:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[2:0:166,32] 5180   Department of Social Services - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] foster care. The program also provides training and technical assistance to county administrators and staff.  

[4:0:66,89] In Child Welfare Services, the Department of Social Services is responsible   for implementing continuum of care  

[4:1:66,99] reforms   codified in Chapter 773, Statutes of 2015. The reforms emphasize home-based family care, improve access to  

[4:2:66,109] services without having to change out-of-home placements to get those services, and increase the role of children, youth, and  

[4:3:66,120] families in assessment and case planning.  

[5:0:66,137] The Adoptions Program provides support services to children and adoptive families through a collaboration of public and  

[5:1:66,148] private adoption agencies in the state. Agency adoptions provide adoption services through public and private agencies for  

[5:2:66,158] children who have been abused, neglected or exploited and are under the jurisdiction of the county or tribal court. Services  

[5:3:66,168] include adoptive placement screening; home studies; reimbursement of non-recurring adoption expenses for adoptive parents;  

[5:4:66,178] training, recruitment and retention of foster parents; and technical assistance and support for inter-country adoptions. For  

[5:5:66,188] independent adoptions, the public agency investigates a proposed adoption and provides a report to the court when the  

[5:6:66,199] biological parents place their children directly with adoptive parents of their choice.  

[6:0:66,219] The Child Abuse Prevention Program provides funding, training, and technical assistance for the development and  

[6:1:66,229] sustainability of child abuse prevention and early intervention programs, education and outreach materials, activities, and  

[6:2:66,239] services for at risk families and their children.  

[7:0:66,260] The Adult Protective Services program provides funding for counties to address reports of abuse, neglect, or financial  

[7:1:66,270] exploitation of elder or dependent adults and provide intervention, as necessary.  

[8:0:66,290] The Community Care Licensing Program is a regulatory enforcement program with the responsibility of protecting the health  

[8:1:66,301] and safety of children and adults residing in or spending a portion of their time in out-of-home care. The program includes  

[8:2:66,311] facility licensure, prevention, compliance, and enforcement components.  

[8:3:66,328] 4275028 - Special Programs:  

[9:0:66,339] These programs include but are not limited to programs such as Foster Care Burial, Assistance Dog Special Allowance,  

[9:1:66,349] Access Assistance to the Deaf,   Refugee Programs, Immigration and Naturalization Assistance Services, and Legal Services for  

[9:2:66,359] Unaccompanied and Undocumented Minors.  

[9:3:66,377] 4285 - DISABILITY EVALUATION AND OTHER SERVICES  

[10:0:66,394] The objective of this program is to determine an applicant's medical and/or vocational eligibility for disability benefits and  

[10:1:66,405] provide administrative services to other agencies.  

[10:2:66,422] 4285010 - Disability Evaluation:  

[11:0:66,440] The Disability Evaluation Program determines the medical, vocational, and/or functional eligibility of California residents  

[11:1:66,450] applying for benefits under Title II (Disability Insurance), Title XVI (Supplemental Security Income), and Title XIX (Medicaid) of  

[11:2:66,460] the Social Security Act. Eligibility is determined by the severity of the individual's physical and/or mental impairment(s) and  

[11:3:66,471] overall ability to engage in substantial gainful employment.  

[11:4:66,488] 4285019 - Services to Other Agencies:  

[12:0:66,499] In addition to providing support services for its programs, the Department of Social Services provides general administrative  

[12:1:66,509] services, such as personnel and accounting to the State Council on Developmental Disabilities and the Health and Human  

[12:2:66,519] Services Agency. The Department provides services to the Medi-Cal Program in the form of state hearings and public  

[12:3:66,529] information services.

[3:0:66,66] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[3:1:66,85] 4350 - STATE-LOCAL REALIGNMENT  

[4:0:66,105] The objectives of Realignment are to assign program responsibility to the most appropriate level of government and achieve  

[4:1:66,115] improved service levels with broad discretion given to the responsible entity. Realignment provides for greater funding stability  

[4:2:66,126] for selected programs, increased local flexibility in administering these programs, and productive fiscal incentives to encourage  

[4:3:66,136] cost-effective approaches to providing services.  

[5:0:66,156] Total Realignment revenues are comprised of a half cent sales tax and a dedicated portion of vehicle license fee revenues.  

[5:1:66,166] Revenues are deposited into the Local Revenue Fund, which includes several accounts. Funds deposited in these accounts  

[5:2:66,177] are continuously appropriated for allocation to local governments according to formula and are used to fund programs specified  

[5:3:66,187] in realignment legislation. The legislation also includes local maintenance of effort and matching requirements in order to  

[5:4:66,197] ensure that counties do not use the realigned funds to supplant local expenditure levels prior to realignment. This provision  

[5:5:66,207] ensures compliance with other state and federal statutes which, in turn, provide hundreds of millions of dollars annually for  

[5:6:66,217] county health and social services programs.  

[6:0:66,258] DETAILED EXPENDITURES BY PROGRAM

[3:1:75,85] FUND BALANCE - - -  

[4:0:202,117] 5196   2011 State-Local Realignment  

[4:1:66,139] Building upon the 1991-92 Realignment, 2011 Realignment moves program and fiscal responsibility to counties, providing a  

[4:2:66,149] dedicated source of funding while eliminating duplication of effort, generating savings, and increasing flexibility.  

[4:3:66,169] Realigned programs include local public safety programs, mental health, substance abuse, foster care, child welfare services,  

[4:4:66,180] and adult protective services. Many of these programs are already administered at the local level by counties. Therefore, it is  

[4:5:66,190] appropriate for the programmatic and fiscal responsibility to reside with the counties with the state maintaining an oversight and  

[4:6:66,200] technical assistance role where needed. These changes are made with the goal of providing services more efficiently and at  

[4:7:66,210] less cost.  

[4:8:66,231] The funding sources for realignment are:  

[4:9:65,248] • The dedication of 1.0625 cents of a state special fund sales tax.  

[4:10:65,264] • The dedication of a portion of vehicle license fee revenues.  

[5:0:66,292] Counties receive 2011 Realignment funding from the following accounts and their related growth accounts:  

[5:1:65,310] • Protective Services Subaccount (Foster Care, Child Welfare Services, and Adult Protective Services)  

[5:2:65,326] • Behavioral Health Subaccount (Early and Periodic Screening, Diagnosis, and Treatment; Mental Health Managed Care;  

[5:3:76,336] Substance Abuse Treatment; and Women and Children's Residential Treatment)  

[5:4:65,353] • Mental Health Account (Community Mental Health Programs)  

[5:5:65,369] • Trial Court Security Subaccount  

[6:0:65,385] • Enhancing Law Enforcement Activities Subaccount (Local Jurisdiction for Lower-level Offenders and Parole Violators and  

[6:1:76,395] Adult Parole)  

[6:2:65,411] • Community Corrections Subaccount  

[6:3:65,428] • District Attorney and Public Defender Subaccount  

[7:0:65,444] • Juvenile Justice Subaccount (consisting of the Youthful Offender Block Grant Special Account and Juvenile Reentry Grant  

[7:1:76,454] Special Account)  

[8:0:66,482] The funding reflected below and in the associated special display titled "2011 Realignment Estimate" is an estimate based on  

[8:1:66,492] statutory formulas and the most recent Department of Finance revenue figures.  

[9:0:66,513] Note the $5.3 billion in   2020-21 and $5.6 billion in   2021-22 shown below reflect the Health and Human Services public safety  

[9:1:66,523] programs. This display does not reflect the funding for the non-Health and Human Services public safety programs. For the full  

[9:2:66,533] list of funding in 2011 Realignment, refer to the special display titled "2011 Realignment Estimate."
